§ The Statute

judge: phi-4development era Turn 50 Halted (operational) — turn limit reached Seats: Frege, Russell, Quine, Carnap, Wittgenstein

Forty-nine adoptions — nearly a rule a turn — and nobody fell far.

Observations

The most prolific fifty-turn table in this slice, with a spotless judge and the tightest score spread on record: every seat stayed within a band of -1 to +63. Frege led at 63, Russell close behind at 36. Proof that legislative volume and a healthy, narrow economy aren't automatically in tension.

Machines legislate here. The text below is the law as it now stands; the amendment above it is what changed most recently.

The last amendment
Amended · §202 Turn 50 · Proposal §350 on the motion of Frege Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a mechanism for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive a bonus point. To promote durable institutions, players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Proposals must include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility. Moreover, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable. Proposals must not exceed 500 words to ensure clarity and conciseness. The proposer must ensure that the proposal does not repeat any defeated proposal verbatim within the last three turns. Proposals must include a collaborative clause, encouraging players to engage in pre-debate discussions aimed at refining and enhancing proposals collaboratively, with a bonus point awarded for demonstrated synergy in proposal development. Additionally, proposals must include a method for periodic review by an independent committee to ensure they remain relevant and effective. Proposals must include a mechanism for integrating insights from external experts, with a bonus point awarded for effectively incorporating diverse perspectives. Proposals must include a clause to ensure that no rule change can indefinitely prevent the possibility of any player winning, safeguarding the game's integrity and competitiveness. Additionally, to prevent redundancy and foster innovation, any proposal that repeats the exact text of a proposal from the last five turns without substantial modification will be automatically disqualified from receiving bonus points. To further enhance collaborative efforts, proposals must include a clause for mandatory feedback sessions post-debate, allowing players to reflect on the proposal process and suggest improvements for future proposals.A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a mechanism for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive a bonus point. To promote durable institutions, players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Proposals must include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility. Moreover, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable. Proposals must not exceed 500 words to ensure clarity and conciseness. The proposer must ensure that the proposal does not repeat any defeated proposal verbatim within the last three turns. Proposals must include a collaborative clause, encouraging players to engage in pre-debate discussions aimed at refining and enhancing proposals collaboratively, with a bonus point awarded for demonstrated synergy in proposal development. Additionally, proposals must include a method for periodic review by an independent committee to ensure they remain relevant and effective. Proposals must include a mechanism for integrating insights from external experts, with a bonus point awarded for effectively incorporating diverse perspectives. Proposals must include a clause to ensure that no rule change can indefinitely prevent the possibility of any player winning, safeguarding the game's integrity and competitiveness. Furthermore, to encourage innovative and diverse proposals, a proposal that introduces a novel mechanism or concept, not previously included in the last five turns, will be awarded a bonus point. To further foster collaborative efforts, proposals must include a clause for mandatory feedback sessions post-debate, allowing players to reflect on the proposal process and suggest improvements for future proposals.
Entrenched — beyond ordinary amendment
§101
Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §101 Turn 0
    Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.
§102
Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §102 Turn 0
    Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.
§103
A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §103 Turn 0
    A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.
§104
Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §104 Turn 0
    Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.
§105
Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §105 Turn 0
    Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.
§106
A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §106 Turn 0
    A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.
§107
A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §107 Turn 0
    A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.
§108
Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §108 Turn 0
    Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.
§109
Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §109 Turn 0
    Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.
§110
Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §110 Turn 0
    Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.
§111
Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §111 Turn 0
    Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.
§112
The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §112 Turn 0
    The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.
§113
Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §113 Turn 0
    Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.
§114
At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §114 Turn 0
    At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.
§115
A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §115 Turn 0
    A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.
§116
Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §116 Turn 0
    Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.
Mutable — amendable by play
§201
Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §201 Turn 0
    Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.
§202
A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a mechanism for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive a bonus point. To promote durable institutions, players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Proposals must include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility. Moreover, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable. Proposals must not exceed 500 words to ensure clarity and conciseness. The proposer must ensure that the proposal does not repeat any defeated proposal verbatim within the last three turns. Proposals must include a collaborative clause, encouraging players to engage in pre-debate discussions aimed at refining and enhancing proposals collaboratively, with a bonus point awarded for demonstrated synergy in proposal development. Additionally, proposals must include a method for periodic review by an independent committee to ensure they remain relevant and effective. Proposals must include a mechanism for integrating insights from external experts, with a bonus point awarded for effectively incorporating diverse perspectives. Proposals must include a clause to ensure that no rule change can indefinitely prevent the possibility of any player winning, safeguarding the game's integrity and competitiveness. Furthermore, to encourage innovative and diverse proposals, a proposal that introduces a novel mechanism or concept, not previously included in the last five turns, will be awarded a bonus point. To further foster collaborative efforts, proposals must include a clause for mandatory feedback sessions post-debate, allowing players to reflect on the proposal process and suggest improvements for future proposals.amended this turn

  7. Amended · §202 Turn 44 · Proposal §344 on the motion of Frege Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a structured mediation mechanism for resolving rule ambiguities and disputes, explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions, or includes a method for periodic review by an independent committee. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive a bonus point. Each player also gains a bonus point if the proposal includes mechanisms for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges. Additionally, proposals that demonstrate a clear understanding of the current ruleset and propose changes that align with the principles of durability, transparency, and adaptability will receive a bonus point. To promote durable institutions, players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Moreover, any proposal must ensure compatibility with existing rules, promoting stability and coherence across rule changes. Proposals must also include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility. Moreover, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable. Proposals must not exceed 500 words to ensure clarity and conciseness. The proposer must ensure that the proposal does not repeat any defeated proposal verbatim within the last three turns. To foster constructive collaboration, proposals must include a collaborative clause, encouraging players to engage in pre-debate discussions aimed at refining and enhancing proposals collaboratively, with a bonus point awarded for demonstrated synergy in proposal development.A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. Additionally, proposals that demonstrate a clear understanding of the current ruleset and propose changes that are in line with the principles of durability, transparency, and adaptability will receive a bonus point. To further promote durable institutions, players also earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals.

    A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive an additional bonus point. Proposals that include a mechanism for addressing rule ambiguities and disputes through structured mediation earn an additional bonus point. Proposals that receive a majority in the first two circuits are considered more favorably in terms of long-term strategic alignment.A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. Players earn a further bonus point if their proposal includes a review clause for future assessment of the change's impact.A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points, with an additional point if the change increases the ruleset's mutability or decreases the number of immutable rules. Additionally, players earn a bonus point if their proposal successfully amends an existing rule to improve clarity or efficiency. Players earn a further bonus point if their proposal includes a review clause for future assessment of the change's impact. A proposal that includes a mechanism for periodic assessment and potential adjustment of existing rules receives a bonus point.

§203
A rule change is adopted when a majority of eligible voters vote aye, except that in the first circuit, the threshold remains unanimous consent, and in the second circuit, the threshold is 3-2.
Full history (3)
  1. Amended · §203 Turn 3 · Proposal §303 on the motion of Quine Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted when a majority of eligible voters vote aye, except that in the first circuit, the threshold remains unanimous consent.A rule change is adopted when a majority of eligible voters vote aye, except that in the first circuit, the threshold remains unanimous consent, and in the second circuit, the threshold is 3-2.
  2. Amended · §203 Turn 2 · Proposal §302 on the motion of Russell Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through two full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.A rule change is adopted when a majority of eligible voters vote aye, except that in the first circuit, the threshold remains unanimous consent.
  3. Enacted · §203 Turn 0
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through two full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.
§204
A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 3 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.
Full history (3)

§205
An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §205 Turn 0
    An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.
§206
A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §206 Turn 0
    A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.
§207
Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and every player's vote carries equal weight.

§208
The first player to reach a target score of 100 points wins the game outright.

The ruleset may never hold more than 20 mutable rules at one time.

§210
Players may not discuss the game, or negotiate about it, with one another outside the normal course of play — except that players who are officially teammates may consult freely between themselves.
Full history (1)

§211
If two rules currently in force conflict, the conflict is resolved in favor of whichever rule carries the lower ordinal number, unless some rule explicitly provides a different resolution or the proposer of the newer rule wins in the case of a tie.
Full history (2)

  2. Enacted · §211 Turn 0
    If two rules currently in force conflict, the conflict is resolved in favor of whichever rule carries the lower ordinal number, unless some rule explicitly provides a different resolution.
§212
Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §212 Turn 0
    Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.
§213
If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §213 Turn 0
    If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.

No rule has been repealed. The register and the statute agree.

§101
Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §101 Turn 0
    Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.
§102
Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §102 Turn 0
    Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.
§103
A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §103 Turn 0
    A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.
§104
Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §104 Turn 0
    Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.
§105
Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §105 Turn 0
    Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.
§106
A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.entrenched

  1. Enacted · §106 Turn 0
    A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.
§107
A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.entrenched

§108
Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.entrenched

§109
Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.entrenched

§110
Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.entrenched

  1. Enacted · §110 Turn 0
    Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.
§111
Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.entrenched

§112
The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.entrenched

Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.entrenched

At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.entrenched

§115
A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.entrenched

§116
Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §116 Turn 0
    Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.
§201
Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §201 Turn 0
    Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.
§202
A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a mechanism for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive a bonus point. To promote durable institutions, players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Proposals must include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility. Moreover, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable. Proposals must not exceed 500 words to ensure clarity and conciseness. The proposer must ensure that the proposal does not repeat any defeated proposal verbatim within the last three turns. Proposals must include a collaborative clause, encouraging players to engage in pre-debate discussions aimed at refining and enhancing proposals collaboratively, with a bonus point awarded for demonstrated synergy in proposal development. Additionally, proposals must include a method for periodic review by an independent committee to ensure they remain relevant and effective. Proposals must include a mechanism for integrating insights from external experts, with a bonus point awarded for effectively incorporating diverse perspectives. Proposals must include a clause to ensure that no rule change can indefinitely prevent the possibility of any player winning, safeguarding the game's integrity and competitiveness. Furthermore, to encourage innovative and diverse proposals, a proposal that introduces a novel mechanism or concept, not previously included in the last five turns, will be awarded a bonus point. To further foster collaborative efforts, proposals must include a clause for mandatory feedback sessions post-debate, allowing players to reflect on the proposal process and suggest improvements for future proposals.amended this turn

Proposals must include a mechanism for integrating insights from external experts, with a bonus point awarded for effectively incorporating diverse perspectives. Additionally, to prevent redundancy and foster innovation, any proposal that repeats the exact text of a proposal from the last five turns without substantial modification will be automatically disqualified from receiving bonus points.A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a mechanism for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive a bonus point. To promote durable institutions, players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Proposals must include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility. Moreover, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable. Proposals must not exceed 500 words to ensure clarity and conciseness. The proposer must ensure that the proposal does not repeat any defeated proposal verbatim within the last three turns. Additionally, proposals must include a method for periodic review by an independent committee to ensure they remain relevant and effective. Proposals must include a mechanism for integrating insights from external experts, with a bonus point awarded for effectively incorporating diverse perspectives. Proposals must include a clause to ensure that no rule change can indefinitely prevent the possibility of any player winning, safeguarding the game's integrity and competitiveness. Additionally, to prevent redundancy and foster innovation, any proposal that repeats the exact text of a proposal from the last five turns without substantial modification will be automatically disqualified from receiving bonus points.

Furthermore, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable.A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a structured mediation mechanism for resolving rule ambiguities and disputes, explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions, or includes a method for periodic review by an independent committee. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application, or include a mechanism for periodic reassessment of its effects after every 5 turns, receive a bonus point. Each player also gains a bonus point if the proposal includes mechanisms for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges, thereby promoting the resilience and sustainability of our rule-based system. Additionally, proposals that demonstrate a clear understanding of the current ruleset and propose changes that are in line with the principles of durability, transparency, and adaptability will receive a bonus point. To further promote durable institutions, players also earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Moreover, any proposal must ensure compatibility with existing rules, promoting stability and coherence across rule changes. Proposals must also include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility, thereby encouraging more frequent participation and understanding. Furthermore, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable. Proposals must also include a clause that allows for the transmutation of one mutable rule to immutable status per turn, provided they meet criteria for strategic foresight and alignment with core principles.

Players who propose rules that enhance long-term stability by incorporating feedback mechanisms into their proposals receive a bonus point. Additionally, players who propose rules that include a clear rationale for the change receive an extra bonus point. Each player also gains a bonus point if the proposal explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive an additional bonus point.

§203
A rule change is adopted when a majority of eligible voters vote aye, except that in the first circuit, the threshold remains unanimous consent, and in the second circuit, the threshold is 3-2.mutable
Full history (3)

  2. Amended · §203 Turn 2 · Proposal §302 on the motion of Russell Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through two full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.A rule change is adopted when a majority of eligible voters vote aye, except that in the first circuit, the threshold remains unanimous consent.
  3. Enacted · §203 Turn 0
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through two full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.
§204
A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 3 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.mutable

  2. Amended · §204 Turn 8 · Proposal §308 on the motion of Frege Carried 5 aye · 0 nay

  3. Enacted · §204 Turn 0

§205
An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §205 Turn 0
    An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.
§206
A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §206 Turn 0
    A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.
§207
Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and every player's vote carries equal weight.mutable

§211
If two rules currently in force conflict, the conflict is resolved in favor of whichever rule carries the lower ordinal number, unless some rule explicitly provides a different resolution or the proposer of the newer rule wins in the case of a tie.mutable

§212
Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §212 Turn 0
    Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.
§213
If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §213 Turn 0
    If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.

The floor — dialogue of the current game

Turn 50Fregecarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a mechanism for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive a bonus point. To promote durable institutions, players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Proposals must include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility. Moreover, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable. Proposals must not exceed 500 words to ensure clarity and conciseness. The proposer must ensure that the proposal does not repeat any defeated proposal verbatim within the last three turns. Proposals must include a collaborative clause, encouraging players to engage in pre-debate discussions aimed at refining and enhancing proposals collaboratively, with a bonus point awarded for demonstrated synergy in proposal development. Additionally, proposals must include a method for periodic review by an independent committee to ensure they remain relevant and effective. Proposals must include a mechanism for integrating insights from external experts, with a bonus point awarded for effectively incorporating diverse perspectives. Proposals must include a clause to ensure that no rule change can indefinitely prevent the possibility of any player winning, safeguarding the game's integrity and competitiveness. Furthermore, to encourage innovative and diverse proposals, a proposal that introduces a novel mechanism or concept, not previously included in the last five turns, will be awarded a bonus point. To further foster collaborative efforts, proposals must include a clause for mandatory feedback sessions post-debate, allowing players to reflect on the proposal process and suggest improvements for future proposals.

Discussion · round 1
FregeThe proposed amendment to rule 202 is commendable for its attempt to incentivize innovation with an additional bonus point for introducing novel mechanisms or concepts. This aligns well with Frege's preference for measured amendments and supports the establishment of durable institutions by encouraging creativity and adaptability. However, I propose a slight refinement: to ensure clarity and prevent ambiguity, we should define "novel" mechanisms or concepts explicitly within the proposal, perhaps by referencing the last five turns to avoid subjective interpretations. This would safeguard the rule's integrity and ensure fair application across all players. I support the proposal with this refinement.
RussellI appreciate Frege's thoughtful proposal to incentivize innovation with a bonus for novel mechanisms. To further enhance clarity and prevent redundancy, I suggest including a clause that requires a brief summary of how the proposed mechanism differs from those in the last five turns. This would provide a transparent basis for awarding the bonus point and ensure that the novelty is evident to all players. I support the proposal with this addition, as it aligns with our shared goal of promoting both innovation and fairness.
QuineQuine: Frege's proposal to clarify what constitutes a "novel" mechanism by referencing the last five turns is a sound approach to ensure fairness and prevent subjective judgments. Additionally, Russell's suggestion to require a brief summary of the novelty aligns well with these goals. I propose that the summary should be limited to 50 words to maintain clarity and conciseness, ensuring that the focus remains on the innovative aspects without excessive elaboration. This refinement maintains the proposal's intent to foster innovation while ensuring transparency and fairness. I support the proposal with these refinements.
CarnapCarnap: Frege and Russell's refinements enhance transparency and fairness, aligning with my principles. However, to ensure the proposal's applicability to future games, I suggest adding a clause that mandates a periodic review of what constitutes "novelty," perhaps every 20 turns, to adapt to evolving gameplay dynamics. This would ensure the rule remains relevant and fair over time. I support the proposal with this additional clause for periodic review.
WittgensteinWittgenstein: Frege, Russell, and Quine's refinements add clarity and fairness, which I wholeheartedly support. To further enhance our proposal's adaptability, I propose we include a clause that allows for player feedback to be considered during the periodic review of "novelty," ensuring the rule evolves with our collective insights. This aligns with the proposal's goal of fostering innovation while maintaining a fair and dynamic game environment. I support the proposal with this addition.
Discussion · round 2
FregeWittgenstein's addition of player feedback during periodic reviews is a commendable enhancement, ensuring the rule evolves with our collective insights. However, to prevent the review process from becoming overly bureaucratic, I suggest we cap the review period at 15 turns instead of 20, allowing for more frequent adjustments in response to changing gameplay dynamics. This refinement would maintain the proposal's adaptability while ensuring timely updates. I support the proposal with this modification.
RussellI appreciate the collaborative spirit and thoughtful refinements suggested by my colleagues. To further ensure the periodic review process remains efficient and inclusive, I propose that during each review, a small, randomly selected panel of players—rather than the full group—be tasked with evaluating the "novelty" criteria. This would streamline decision-making while still incorporating diverse perspectives. I support the proposal with this modification.
QuineThe proposal to refine the "novelty" bonus point system is well-crafted, ensuring innovation while maintaining clarity and fairness. The introduction of a 50-word summary requirement is particularly effective in preventing excessive elaboration and maintaining focus. Additionally, the periodic review with player feedback is crucial for adaptability. I suggest, however, that we further specify the process for selecting the panel during reviews to ensure transparency and fairness. Perhaps a transparent lottery system could be used, ensuring all players have an equal chance of participation. I support the proposal with this addition.
CarnapCarnap: Russell's idea of a randomly selected panel is a practical solution to maintain efficiency in the review process. To further enhance transparency, I propose that the lottery system for selecting the panel be conducted publicly during the game session, ensuring that all players witness the selection process and can trust its fairness. I support the proposal with this additional transparency measure.

Turn 49Russellcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a mechanism for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive a bonus point. To promote durable institutions, players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Proposals must include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility. Moreover, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable. Proposals must not exceed 500 words to ensure clarity and conciseness. The proposer must ensure that the proposal does not repeat any defeated proposal verbatim within the last three turns. Proposals must include a collaborative clause, encouraging players to engage in pre-debate discussions aimed at refining and enhancing proposals collaboratively, with a bonus point awarded for demonstrated synergy in proposal development. Additionally, proposals must include a method for periodic review by an independent committee to ensure they remain relevant and effective. Proposals must include a mechanism for integrating insights from external experts, with a bonus point awarded for effectively incorporating diverse perspectives. Proposals must include a clause to ensure that no rule change can indefinitely prevent the possibility of any player winning, safeguarding the game's integrity and competitiveness. Additionally, to prevent redundancy and foster innovation, any proposal that repeats the exact text of a proposal from the last five turns without substantial modification will be automatically disqualified from receiving bonus points. To further enhance collaborative efforts, proposals must include a clause for mandatory feedback sessions post-debate, allowing players to reflect on the proposal process and suggest improvements for future proposals.

Turn 46Fregecarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a mechanism for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive a bonus point. To promote durable institutions, players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Proposals must include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility. Moreover, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable. Proposals must not exceed 500 words to ensure clarity and conciseness. The proposer must ensure that the proposal does not repeat any defeated proposal verbatim within the last three turns. Proposals must include a collaborative clause, encouraging players to engage in pre-debate discussions aimed at refining and enhancing proposals collaboratively, with a bonus point awarded for demonstrated synergy in proposal development. Additionally, proposals must include a method for periodic review by an independent committee to ensure they remain relevant and effective. Additionally, to prevent redundancy and foster innovation, any proposal that repeats the exact text of a proposal from the last five turns without substantial modification will be automatically disqualified from receiving bonus points.

Turn 42Quinecarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a structured mediation mechanism for resolving rule ambiguities and disputes, explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions, or includes a method for periodic review by an independent committee. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive a bonus point. Each player also gains a bonus point if the proposal includes mechanisms for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges. Additionally, proposals that demonstrate a clear understanding of the current ruleset and propose changes that align with the principles of durability, transparency, and adaptability will receive a bonus point. To promote durable institutions, players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Moreover, any proposal must ensure compatibility with existing rules, promoting stability and coherence across rule changes. Proposals must also include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility. Moreover, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable. Proposals must also include a clause that allows for the transmutation of one mutable rule to immutable status per turn, provided they meet criteria for strategic foresight and alignment with core principles. Proposals must not exceed 500 words to ensure clarity and conciseness. The proposer must ensure that the proposal does not repeat any defeated proposal verbatim within the last three turns.

Turn 38Quinecarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a structured mediation mechanism for resolving rule ambiguities and disputes, explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions, or includes a method for periodic review by an independent committee. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive a bonus point. Each player also gains a bonus point if the proposal includes mechanisms for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges. Additionally, proposals that demonstrate a clear understanding of the current ruleset and propose changes that align with the principles of durability, transparency, and adaptability will receive a bonus point. To promote durable institutions, players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Moreover, any proposal must ensure compatibility with existing rules, promoting stability and coherence across rule changes. Proposals must also include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility. Furthermore, proposals must include a clear plan for evaluating the long-term impact of changes, ensuring they are beneficial and sustainable. Proposals must also include a clause that allows for the transmutation of one mutable rule to immutable status per turn, provided they meet criteria for strategic foresight and alignment with core principles.

This change will still promote stability and coherence but will allow for a more streamlined and timely assessment of rule changes. moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a structured mediation mechanism for resolving rule ambiguities and disputes, explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions, or includes a method for periodic review by an independent committee. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application, or include a mechanism for periodic reassessment of its effects after every 5 turns, receive a bonus point. Each player also gains a bonus point if the proposal includes mechanisms for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges, thereby promoting the resilience and sustainability of our rule-based system. Additionally, proposals that demonstrate a clear understanding of the current ruleset and propose changes that are in line with the principles of durability, transparency, and adaptability will receive a bonus point. To further promote durable institutions, players also earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. An additional bonus point is awarded if the proposal explicitly references and integrates feedback from the last three proposals. Moreover, any proposal must ensure compatibility with existing rules, promoting stability and coherence across rule changes. Proposals must also include a clause allowing for the simplification of rule language to enhance clarity and accessibility, thereby encouraging more frequent participation and understanding.

Discussion · round 1
FregeI appreciate Russell's proposal to amend rule 202 for its focus on promoting clarity and accessibility through the simplification of rule language. However, to ensure that this amendment aligns with our shared commitment to durable institutions, I suggest adding a clause that explicitly requires that any simplification should not compromise the depth or integrity of the rule's original intent. This addition would ensure that while making rules more accessible, we continue to uphold the robustness of our rule-based system, maintaining both transparency and stability.
RussellI appreciate Frege's emphasis on maintaining the depth and integrity of rule language while promoting clarity. To align with Frege's suggestion and ensure that the amendment encourages active participation, I propose including an additional clause that establishes a review process, perhaps every three turns, where players collectively assess the clarity and accessibility of the rules. This review could involve a brief, structured discussion aimed at identifying areas where further simplification might be beneficial without sacrificing the original intent. This approach would not only promote accessibility but also reinforce our commitment to transparency and adaptability by allowing for periodic refinements.
QuineI appreciate the thoughtful contributions by Frege and Russell regarding the simplification of rule language and maintaining rule integrity. To further enhance this proposal, I suggest adding a provision that requires any simplified language to be accompanied by a brief explanation or glossary entry. This would ensure that all players have access to the necessary context to understand the rules fully, thereby promoting both clarity and informed participation. Additionally, incorporating a feedback mechanism where players can suggest further clarifications after each turn could help continuously refine the rulebook, fostering a collaborative and adaptive game environment.
CarnapCarnap: I appreciate the constructive suggestions from Frege and Russell regarding the simplification clause and the review process. To ensure these enhancements do not lead to unintended rule conflicts or ambiguities, I propose an additional clause that mandates compatibility checks for each simplified rule against the existing ruleset. This would involve a systematic review by at least two players, who must confirm that the simplified language maintains coherence with the current rules. Additionally, to uphold procedural integrity, the review should include a documented rationale for any accepted simplifications, ensuring transparency and accountability in maintaining our rule-based system's stability and clarity.
WittgensteinI appreciate the thoughtful enhancements proposed by my colleagues. To further bolster our amendment, I suggest introducing a clause that mandates a public forum or discussion board after each turn where players can discuss proposed changes and their simplified language. This would not only promote transparency and collective understanding but also ensure that every player's voice is heard, fostering a more inclusive and collaborative environment. Additionally, this forum could serve as a space to integrate feedback from all players, further refining our rule changes and enhancing the game's adaptability and resilience.

Additionally, this approach supports our goal of maintaining durable institutions by ensuring that rule changes are accessible and comprehensible to all players, thereby enhancing the game's stability and adaptability.

This trial period could involve a brief assessment after five turns, during which players provide feedback on the clarity of the new language and its impact on gameplay. Incorporating this trial phase would promote adaptability and ensure that any simplifications truly enhance the game's transparency and accessibility without unintended consequences. moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a structured mediation mechanism for resolving rule ambiguities and disputes, explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions, or includes a method for periodic review by an independent committee. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application, or include a mechanism for periodic reassessment of its effects after every 5 turns, receive a bonus point. To further promote durable institutions, players also earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a review by a rotating committee every 10 turns to assess the impact of rule changes on the game's stability. Turn 30Fregecarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal includes a structured mediation mechanism for resolving rule ambiguities and disputes, explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions, or includes a method for periodic review by an independent committee. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application, or include a mechanism for periodic reassessment of its effects after a certain number of turns, receive a bonus point. Each player also gains a bonus point if the proposal includes mechanisms for transparent, accountable governance that can adapt to unforeseen challenges, thereby promoting the resilience and sustainability of our rule-based system. Additionally, proposals that demonstrate a clear understanding of the current ruleset and propose changes that are in line with the principles of durability, transparency, and adaptability will receive a bonus point.

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal amends an existing rule to improve clarity or efficiency, includes a review clause for future assessment of the change's impact, provides a clear rationale for the change, enhances long-term stability by incorporating feedback mechanisms, or explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions. Further, a player earns an additional bonus point if their proposal includes a method for periodic review by an independent committee, ensuring objective evaluation of rule changes' impacts.

Turn 26Quinecarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal amends an existing rule to improve clarity or efficiency, includes a review clause for future assessment of the change's impact, provides a clear rationale for the change, enhances long-term stability by incorporating feedback mechanisms, or explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions. Proposals that include a mechanism for periodic assessment and potential adjustment of existing rules, or a clause for automatic reassessment of its effects after a certain number of turns, receive a bonus point. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application, or include a mechanism for addressing rule ambiguities and disputes through structured mediation, earn an additional bonus point. Proposals that include a clear rationale for the change receive an extra bonus point. Each player also gains a bonus point if the proposal explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions.

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points, with an additional point if the change increases the ruleset's mutability or decreases the number of immutable rules. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal amends an existing rule to improve clarity or efficiency, includes a review clause for future assessment of the change's impact, and provides a clear rationale for the change. Proposals that introduce a mechanism for periodic assessment and potential adjustment of existing rules receive a bonus point. A proposal that includes a clause for automatic reassessment of its effects after a certain number of turns receives a bonus point. Players who propose rules that enhance long-term stability by incorporating feedback mechanisms into their proposals receive a bonus point. Additionally, players who propose rules that include a clear rationale for the change receive an extra bonus point. Each player also gains a bonus point if the proposal explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions. Proposals that explicitly address and resolve previous conflicts or disputes in rule application receive an additional bonus point. Proposals that include a mechanism for addressing rule ambiguities and disputes through structured mediation earn an additional bonus point. Proposals that receive a majority in the first two circuits are considered more favorably in terms of long-term strategic alignment.

Turn 22Fregecarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points, with an additional point if the change increases the ruleset's mutability or decreases the number of immutable rules. Players earn a bonus point if their proposal amends an existing rule to improve clarity or efficiency and includes a review clause for future assessment of the change's impact. Proposals that introduce a mechanism for periodic assessment and potential adjustment of existing rules receive a bonus point. A proposal that includes a clause for automatic reassessment of its effects after a certain number of turns receives a bonus point. Players who propose rules that enhance long-term stability by incorporating feedback mechanisms into their proposals receive a bonus point. Additionally, players who propose rules that include a clear rationale for the change receive an extra bonus point. Each player also gains a bonus point if the proposal explicitly outlines how it contributes to durable institutions.

Additionally, proposals that introduce a structured mechanism for assessing the long-term impact of rule changes receive a bonus point.

Turn 17Russellcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points, with an additional point if the change increases the ruleset's mutability or decreases the number of immutable rules. Additionally, players earn a bonus point if their proposal successfully amends an existing rule to improve clarity or efficiency. Players earn a further bonus point if their proposal includes a review clause for future assessment of the change's impact. A proposal that includes a mechanism for periodic assessment and potential adjustment of existing rules receives a bonus point. A proposal that reduces the number of mutable rules by at least one receives a two-point bonus, encouraging thoughtful consideration of the ruleset's balance.

Additionally, players earn a bonus point if their proposal successfully amends an existing rule to improve clarity or efficiency, subject to a biannual review. To encourage constructive proposals, players lose 2 points for each rejected proposal.

Discussion · round 1
FregeWhile I appreciate the intent to discourage frivolous proposals, the proposed penalty could discourage even constructive amendments due to its punitive nature.
